Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-631 District clerk -- Meetings and records.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-631(1): The board of trustees of each special district shall appoint a district clerk.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-631(2): If required, the clerk may be chosen from among the members of the board of trustees, except the chair.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-631(3): The district clerk or other appointed person shall attend the meetings and keep a record of the proceedings of the board of trustees.


Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-632 District clerk -- Bookkeeping duties.
---------------------------------------------------------------------
The district clerk or other designated person not performing treasurer duties shall maintain the financial records for each fund of the special district and all related subsidiary records, including a list of the outstanding bonds, their purpose, amount, terms, date, and place payable.

Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-633 District treasurer -- Duties generally.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-633(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-633(1)(a): The board of trustees of each special district shall appoint a district treasurer.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-633(1)(b): 
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-633(1)(b)(i): If required, the treasurer may be chosen from among the members of the board of trustees, except that the board chair may not be district treasurer.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-633(1)(b)(ii): The district clerk may not also be the district treasurer.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-633(2): The district treasurer is custodian of all money, bonds, or other securities of the district.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-633(3): Title 51, Chapter 7, State Money Management Act; (3)(b) The district treasurer shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-633(3)(a): Title 51, Chapter 7, State Money Management Act determine the cash requirements of the district and provide for the deposit and investment of all money by following the procedures and requirements of
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-633(3)(b): receive all public funds and money payable to the district within three business days after collection, including all taxes, licenses, fines, and intergovernmental revenue;
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-633(3)(c): (3)(b) keep an accurate detailed account of all money received under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-633(3)(d): collect all special taxes and assessments as provided by law and ordinance.


Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-634 Receipts for payment.
-----------------------------------------------------
The district treasurer shall give or cause to be given to every person paying money to the district treasury, a receipt or other evidence of payment, specifying, as appropriate, the date of payment and upon which account paid and shall file the duplicate of the receipt.

Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-635 Duties with respect to issuance of checks.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-635(1): 17B-1-642 The district clerk or other designated person not performing treasurer duties shall prepare the necessary checks after having determined that:
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-635(1)(a): 17B-1-642 the claim was authorized by:
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-635(1)(a)(i): the board of trustees; or

Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-635(2):

Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-636 Special assessments -- Application of proceeds.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------
All money received by the treasurer on any special assessment shall be applied to the payment of the improvement for which the assessment was made.  The money shall be used for the payment of interest and principal on bonds or other indebtedness issued in settlement, and may not be used for any other purpose except as provided in Section

Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-637 Deposit of district funds -- Commingling with personal funds unlawful -- Suspension from office.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
The treasurer shall promptly deposit all district funds in the appropriate bank accounts of the district.  It shall be unlawful for any person to commingle district funds with the person's own money.  If it appears that the treasurer or any other officer is making a profit out of public money, or is using the same for any purpose not authorized by law, the treasurer or officer shall be suspended from office.

Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-638 Quarterly financial reports required.
---------------------------------------------------------------------
The district clerk or other delegated person shall prepare and present to the board of trustees detailed quarterly financial reports showing the financial position and operations of the district for that quarter and the year to date status.

Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-639 Annual financial reports -- Audit reports.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-639(1): Within 180 days after the close of each fiscal year, the district shall prepare an annual financial report in conformity with generally accepted accounting principles as prescribed in the Uniform Accounting Manual for Special Districts.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-639(2): (1) The requirement under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-639(3): Copies of the annual financial report or the audit report furnished by the auditor shall be filed with the state auditor and shall be filed as a public document in the district office.

Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-644 Definitions -- Electronic payments -- Fee.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-644(1): As used in this section:
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-644(1)(a): "Electronic payment" means the payment of money to a special district by electronic means, including by means of a credit card, charge card, debit card, prepaid or stored value card or similar device, or automatic clearinghouse transaction.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-644(1)(b): "Electronic payment fee" means an amount of money to defray the discount fee, processing fee, or other fee charged by a credit card company or processing agent to process an electronic payment.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-644(1)(c): "Processing agent" means a bank, transaction clearinghouse, or other third party that charges a fee to process an electronic payment.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-644(2): A special district may accept an electronic payment for the payment of funds which the special district could have received through another payment method.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-644(3): A special district that accepts an electronic payment may charge an electronic payment fee.


Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-645 Residential fee credit.
-------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-645(1): A special district may create a fee structure under this title that permits:
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-645(1)(a): a home owner or residential tenant to file for a fee credit for a fee charged by the special district, if the credit is based on:
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-645(1)(a)(i): the home owner's annual income; or
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-645(1)(a)(ii): the residential tenant's annual income; or
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-645(1)(b): an owner of federally subsidized housing to file for a credit for a fee charged by the special district.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-645(2): (1)(a) If a special district permits a person to file for a fee credit under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-645(2)(a): a home owner; and
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-645(2)(b): a residential tenant.


Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-701 Definitions.
--------------------------------------------
As used in this part:Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-701(1): Title 51, Chapter 2a, Accounting Reports from Political Subdivisions, Interlocal Organizations, and Other Local Entities Act "Audit reports" means the reports of any independent audit of the district performed by:
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-701(1)(a): Title 51, Chapter 2a, Accounting Reports from Political Subdivisions, Interlocal Organizations, and Other Local Entities Act an independent auditor as required by
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-701(1)(b): the state auditor; or
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-701(1)(c): the legislative auditor.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-701(2): "Board" means the special district board of trustees.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-701(3): "Budget" means a plan of financial operations for a fiscal year that includes:
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-701(3)(a): estimates of proposed expenditures for given purposes and the proposed means of financing them;
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-701(3)(b): the source and amount of estimated revenue for the district for the fiscal year;
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-701(3)(c): fund balance in each fund at the beginning of the fiscal year and the projected fund balance for each fund at the end of the fiscal year; and
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-701(3)(d): capital projects or budgets for proposed construction or improvement to capital facilities within the district.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-701(4): "Constituent entity" means any county, city, or town that levies property taxes within the boundaries of the district.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-701(5): 
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-701(5)(a): "Customer agencies" means those governmental entities, except school districts, institutions of higher education, and federal government agencies that purchase or obtain services from the special district.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-701(5)(b): "Customer agencies" for purposes of state agencies means the state auditor.


Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-702 Special districts to submit budgets.
--------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-702(1): (1)(b); 17B-2a-802
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-702(1)(a): (1)(b) Except as provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-702(1)(a)(i): each of its constituent entities that has in writing requested a copy; and
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-702(1)(a)(ii): to each of its customer agencies that has in writing requested a copy.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-702(1)(b): 17B-2a-802 Within 30 days after it is approved by the board, and at least 30 days before the board adopts a final budget, the board of trustees of a large public transit district as defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-702(1)(b)(i): each of its constituent entities;
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-702(1)(b)(ii): each of its customer agencies that has in writing requested a copy;
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-702(1)(b)(iii): the governor; and
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-702(1)(b)(iv): the Legislature.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-702(1)(c): The special district shall include with the tentative budget a signature sheet that includes:
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-702(1)(c)(i): language that the constituent entity or customer agency received the tentative budget and has no objection to it; and
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-702(1)(c)(ii): a place for the chairperson or other designee of the constituent entity or customer agency to sign.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-702(2): Each constituent entity and each customer agency that receives the tentative budget shall review the tentative budget submitted by the district and either:
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-702(2)(a): sign the signature sheet and return it to the district; or
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-702(2)(b): attend the budget hearing or other meeting scheduled by the district to discuss the objections to the proposed budget.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-702(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-702(3)(a): If any constituent entity or customer agency that received the tentative budget has not returned the signature sheet to the special district within 15 calendar days after the tentative budget was mailed, the special district shall send a written notice of the budget hearing to each constituent entity or customer agency that did not return a signature sheet and invite them to attend that hearing.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-702(3)(b): If requested to do so by any constituent entity or customer agency, the special district shall schedule a meeting to discuss the budget with the constituent entities and customer agencies.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-702(3)(c): At the budget hearing, the special district board shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-702(3)(c)(i): explain its budget and answer any questions about it;
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-702(3)(c)(ii): specifically address any questions or objections raised by the constituent entity, customer agency, or those attending the meeting; and
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-702(3)(c)(iii): seek to resolve the objections.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-702(4): Nothing in this part prevents a special district board from approving or implementing a budget over any or all constituent entity's or customer agency's protests, objections, or failure to respond.

Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-703(1)(a)(ii): each of its customer agencies that has in writing requested a copy.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-703(1)(b): 17B-2a-802 Within 30 days after it is presented to the board, the board of a large public transit district as defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-703(1)(b)(i): each of its constituent entities; and
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-703(1)(b)(ii): each of its customer agencies that has in writing requested a copy.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-703(2): Each constituent entity and each customer agency that received the audit report shall review the audit report submitted by the district and, if necessary, request a meeting with the district board to discuss the audit report.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-703(3): At the meeting, the special district board shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-703(3)(a): answer any questions about the audit report; and
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-703(3)(b): discuss their plans to implement suggestions made by the auditor.


Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-801 Establishment of special district merit system.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-801(1): A merit system of personnel administration for the special districts of the state, their departments, offices, and agencies, except as otherwise specifically provided, is established.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-801(2): This part does not apply to a special district with annual revenues less than $50,000.


Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-802 Review of personnel policies.
-------------------------------------------------------------
Each special district that has full or part-time employees shall annually review its personnel policies to ensure that they conform to the requirements of state and federal law.

Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-803 Merit principles.
-------------------------------------------------
A special district may establish a personnel system administered in a manner that will provide for the effective implementation of merit principles that provide for:Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-803(1): recruiting, selecting, and advancing employees on the basis of their relative ability, knowledge, and skills, including open consideration of qualified applicants for initial appointment;
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-803(2): providing equitable and adequate compensation;
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-803(3): training employees as needed to assure high-quality performance;
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-803(4): retaining employees on the basis of the adequacy of their performance, and separation of employees whose inadequate performance cannot be corrected;
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-803(5): fair treatment of applicants and employees in all aspects of personnel administration without regard to race, color, religion, sex, national origin, political affiliation, age, or disability, and with proper regard for their privacy and constitutional rights as citizens;
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-803(6): providing information to employees regarding their political rights and prohibited practices under the Hatch Political Activities Act, 5 U.S.C. Sec. 1501 through 1508 et seq.; and
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-803(7): providing a formal procedure for processing the appeals and grievances of employees without discrimination, coercion, restraint, or reprisal.

------------------------------------------------------------------------
Each special district shall comply with the requirements of Section

Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-902.1 Interest -- Collection of administrative costs.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-902.1(1): (1)(b)
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-902.1(1)(a): A special district may charge interest on a past due fee or past due charge.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-902.1(1)(b): (1)(b) If a special district charges interest as described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-902.1(1)(b)(i): based on the federal short-term rate determined by the secretary of the treasury under Section 6621, Internal Revenue Code, in effect for the preceding fourth calendar quarter; and
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-902.1(1)(b)(ii): as simple interest at the rate of eighteen percentage points above the federal short-term rate.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-902.1(1)(c): If a special district charges interest on a past due fee collected by the special district, regardless of whether the fee is certified, the special district may charge the interest monthly but may not compound the interest more frequently than annually.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-902.1(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-902.1(2)(a): A special district may charge and collect only one of the following:
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-902.1(2)(a)(i): a one-time penalty charge not to exceed 8% for a past-due fee; or
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-902.1(2)(a)(ii): an administrative cost for some or all of the following:
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-902.1(2)(a)(ii)(A): the collection cost of a past due fee or charge;
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-902.1(2)(a)(ii)(B): reasonable attorney fees actually incurred for collection and foreclosure costs, if applicable; and
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-902.1(2)(a)(ii)(C): any other cost.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-902.1(2)(b): A special district may not charge interest on an administrative cost.

Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-905 Right of entry on premises of water user.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------
A person authorized by a special district that provides a service from a water system or sewer system may enter upon a premise furnished with or provided that water service or sewer service to:Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-905(1): examine an apparatus related to or used by the water system or sewer system;
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-905(2): examine the amount of water used or wastewater discharged by the water system or sewer system and the manner of use or discharge; or
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-905(3): make a necessary shutoff for vacancy, delinquency, or a violation of a special district rule or regulation relating to the water service or sewer service.

Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1104 Pledge of revenues to pay for bonds.
---------------------------------------------------------------------
Bonds may be payable from and secured by the pledge of all or any specified part of:Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1104(1): the revenues to be derived by the special district from providing its services and from the operation of its facilities and other properties;
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1104(2): sales and use taxes, property taxes, and other taxes;
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1104(3): federal, state, or local grants;
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1104(4): in the case of special assessment bonds, the special assessments pledged to repay the special assessment bonds; and
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1104(5): other money legally available to the district.


Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1105 Revenue bonds -- Requirement to impose rates and charges to cover revenue bonds -- Authority to make agreements and covenants to provide for bond repayment.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1105(1): Title 11, Chapter 14, Local Government Bonding Act A special district intending to issue revenue bonds may, but is not required to, submit to district voters for their approval the issuance of the revenue bonds at an election held for that purpose as provided in
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1105(2): Each special district that has issued revenue bonds shall impose rates and charges for the services or commodities it provides fully sufficient, along with other sources of district revenues, to carry out all undertakings of the district with respect to its revenue bonds.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1105(3): 17B-1-103(2)(g); Title 11, Chapter 14, Local Government Bonding Act A special district that issues revenue bonds may:
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1105(3)(a): 17B-1-103(2)(g) agree to pay operation and maintenance expenses of the district from the proceeds of the ad valorem taxes authorized in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1105(3)(b): Title 11, Chapter 14, Local Government Bonding Act for the benefit of bondholders, enter into covenants that:
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1105(3)(b)(i): Title 11, Chapter 14, Local Government Bonding Act are permitted by
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1105(3)(b)(ii): provide for other pertinent matters that the board of trustees considers proper to assure the marketability of the bonds.


Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1106 Board of trustees required to fix rates to cover district expenses and bonds.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
The board of trustees shall fix the rate or rates for services or commodities provided by the district that will, in conjunction with the proceeds of any maintenance and operation tax and other district revenues:Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1106(1): pay the district's operating expenses;
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1106(2): provide for repairs and depreciation of works owned or operated by the district;
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1106(3): pay the interest on any bonds issued by the district; and
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1106(4): provide, as much as practicable, a sinking or other fund to pay the principal of the bonds as they become due.


Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1107 Ratification of previously issued bonds and previously entered contracts.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
All bonds issued or contracts entered into by a special district before April 30, 2007 are ratified, validated, and confirmed and declared to be valid and legally binding obligations of the district in accordance with their terms.

Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1201 Definitions.
---------------------------------------------
As used in this part:Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1201(1): "Eligible function" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1201(1)(a): a power conferred on a special district under this title;
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1201(1)(b): a tax or assessment levied by a special district;
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1201(1)(c): an act or proceeding that a special district:
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1201(1)(c)(i): has taken; or
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1201(1)(c)(ii): contemplates taking; or
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1201(1)(d): a district contract, whether already executed or to be executed in the future, including a contract for the acquisition, construction, maintenance, or operation of works for the district.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1201(2): "Validation order" means a court order adjudicating the validity of an eligible function.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1201(3): "Validation petition" means a petition requesting a validation order.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1201(4): "Validation proceedings" means judicial proceedings occurring in district court pursuant to a validation petition.


Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1202 Authority to file a validation petition -- Petition requirements -- Amending or supplementing a validation petition.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1202(1): The board of trustees of a special district may at any time file a validation petition.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1202(2): Each validation petition shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1202(2)(a): describe the eligible function for which a validation order is sought;
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1202(2)(b): set forth:
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1202(2)(b)(i): the facts upon which the validity of the eligible function is founded; and
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1202(2)(b)(ii): any other information or allegations necessary to a determination of the validation petition;
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1202(2)(c): be verified by the chair of the board of trustees; and
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1202(2)(d): be filed in the district court of the county in which the district's principal office is located.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1202(3): 17B-1-1203; 17B-1-1203 A special district may amend or supplement a validation petition:
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1202(3)(a): 17B-1-1203 at any time before the hearing under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1202(3)(b): 17B-1-1203 after the hearing under Section

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1206 Validation petition hearing -- Validation proceedings.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1206(1): At each validation petition hearing, the court shall determine all matters and issues affecting the questions raised by the validation petition.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1206(2): The district court shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1206(2)(a): advance each matter pertaining to validation proceedings as a matter of immediate public interest and concern; and
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1206(2)(b): hear each matter pertaining to validation proceedings at the earliest practicable moment.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1206(3): The district court shall disregard each error, irregularity, or omission that does not affect the substantial rights of the parties.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1206(4): Except as otherwise specified in this part, the Utah Rules of Civil Procedure shall govern validation proceedings in matters of pleading and practice before the district court.


Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1207 Findings, conclusions, and judgment -- Costs -- Effect of judgment -- Appeal.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1207(1): 17B-1-1203 After the hearing under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1207(1)(a): make and enter written findings of fact and conclusions of law; and
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1207(1)(b): render a judgment as warranted.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1207(2): A district court may apportion costs among the parties as the court determines appropriate.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1207(3): A district court judgment adjudicating matters raised by a validation petition:
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1207(3)(a): is binding and conclusive as to the special district and all other parties to the validation proceedings; and
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1207(3)(b): constitutes a permanent injunction against any action or proceeding to contest any matter adjudicated in the validation proceedings.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1207(4): 
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1207(4)(a): Each appeal of a final judgment in validation proceedings shall be filed with the Supreme Court.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1207(4)(b): An appeal of a final judgment in validation proceedings may be filed only by a party to the validation proceedings.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1207(4)(c): The appellate court hearing an appeal under this section shall expedite the hearing of the appeal.


Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1301 Definitions.
---------------------------------------------
For purposes of this part:Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1301(1): "Active" means, with respect to a special district, that the district is not inactive.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1301(2): (2)(a) "Administrative body" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1301(2)(a): if the special district proposed to be dissolved has a duly constituted board of trustees in sufficient numbers to form a quorum, the board of trustees; or
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1301(2)(b): (2)(a) except as provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1301(2)(b)(i): for a special district located entirely within a single municipality, the legislative body of that municipality;
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1301(2)(b)(ii): for a special district located in multiple municipalities within the same county or at least partly within the unincorporated area of a county, the legislative body of that county; or
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1301(2)(b)(iii): for a special district located within multiple counties, the legislative body of the county whose boundaries include more of the special district than is included within the boundaries of any other county.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1301(3): (2)(a); (2)(b)(i); (2)(b)(ii); (iii) "Clerk" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1301(3)(a): (2)(a) the board of trustees if the board is also the administrative body under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1301(3)(b): (2)(b)(i) the clerk or recorder of the municipality whose legislative body is the administrative body under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1301(3)(c): (2)(b)(ii); (iii) the clerk of the county whose legislative body is the administrative body under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1301(4): "Inactive" means, with respect to a special district, that during the preceding three years the district has not:
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1301(4)(a): provided any service or otherwise operated;
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1301(4)(b): received property taxes or user or other fees; and
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1301(4)(c): expended any funds.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1301(5): 17B-1-1303(1)(a)(ii)(B); 17B-1-1303(2)(c)(ii) "Registered voter petition" means petition under Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1302 Special district dissolution.
--------------------------------------------------------------
A special district may be dissolved as provided in this part.

Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1303 Initiation of dissolution process.
-------------------------------------------------------------------
The process to dissolve a special district may be initiated by:Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1303(1): for an inactive special district:
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1303(1)(a): 
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1303(1)(a)(i): for a special district whose board of trustees is elected by electors based on the acre-feet of water allotted to the land owned by the elector, a petition signed by the owners of 25% of the acre-feet of water allotted to the land within the special district; or
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1303(1)(a)(ii): for all other districts:
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1303(1)(a)(ii)(A): a petition signed by the owners of private real property that:
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1303(1)(a)(ii)(A)(I): is located within the special district proposed to be dissolved;
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1303(1)(a)(ii)(A)(II): covers at least 25% of the private land area within the special district; and
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1303(1)(a)(ii)(A)(III): is equal in assessed value to at least 25% of the assessed value of all private real property within the special district; or
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1303(1)(a)(ii)(B): a petition signed by registered voters residing within the special district proposed to be dissolved equal in number to at least 25% of the number of votes cast in the district for the office of governor at the last regular general election before the filing of the petition; or
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1303(1)(b): a resolution adopted by the administrative body; and
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1303(2): 73-5-15 for an active special district, a petition signed by:
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1303(2)(a): for a special district whose board of trustees is elected by electors based on the acre-feet of water allotted to the land owned by the elector, the owners of 33% of the acre-feet of water allotted to the land within the special district;
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1303(2)(b): 73-5-15 for a special district created to acquire or assess a groundwater right for the development and execution of a groundwater management plan in coordination with the state engineer in accordance with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1303(2)(b)(i): are diverted within the district; and
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1303(2)(b)(ii): cover at least 33% of the total amount of groundwater diverted in accordance with the groundwater rights within the district as a whole; or
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1303(2)(c): for all other districts:
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1303(2)(c)(i): the owners of private real property that:
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1303(2)(c)(i)(A): is located within the special district proposed to be dissolved;
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1303(2)(c)(i)(B): covers at least 33% of the private land area within the special district; and
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1303(2)(c)(i)(C): is equal in assessed value to at least 25% of the assessed value of all private real property within the special district; or
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-1-1303(2)(c)(ii): 33% of registered voters residing within the special district proposed to be dissolved.

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-201 Title.
---------------------------------------
This part is known as the "Drainage District Act."

Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-202 Definitions.
---------------------------------------------
As used in this part:Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-202(1): "Ditch" includes a drain or natural or constructed watercourse, whether open, covered, or tiled, and whether inside or outside the drainage district.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-202(2): "Drainage" includes the reclamation, protection, or betterment of land by leading, carrying, withholding, or pumping excess water from land through canals, ditches, pipes, or other means.


Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-203 Provisions applicable to drainage districts.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-203(1): Chapter 1, Provisions Applicable to All Special Districts Each drainage district is governed by and has the powers stated in:
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-203(1)(a): this part; and
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-203(1)(b): Chapter 1, Provisions Applicable to All Special Districts
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-203(2): This part applies only to drainage districts.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-203(3): A drainage district is not subject to the provisions of any other part of this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-203(4): Chapter 1, Provisions Applicable to All Special Districts If there is a conflict between a provision in


Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-204 Prohibition against creating a drainage district.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------
No new drainage district may be created.

Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-205 Additional drainage district powers.
---------------------------------------------------------------------
In addition to the powers conferred on a drainage district under SectionUtah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-205(1): enter upon land for the purpose of examining the land or making a survey;
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-205(2): locate a necessary drainage canal with any necessary branches on land that the district's board of trustees considers best;
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-205(3): Chapter 1, Part 11, Special District Bonds issue bonds as provided in and subject to
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-205(4): after the payment or tender of compensation allowed, go upon land to construct proposed works, and thereafter enter upon that land to maintain or repair the works;
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-205(5): appropriate water for useful and beneficial purposes;
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-205(6): regulate and control, for the benefit of landholders within the district, all water developed, appropriated, or owned by the district;
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-205(7): appropriate, use, purchase, develop, sell, and convey water and water rights in the same manner and for the same use and purposes as a private person;
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-205(8): widen, straighten, deepen, enlarge, or remove any obstruction or rubbish from any watercourse, whether inside or outside the district; and
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-205(9): if necessary, straighten a watercourse by cutting a new channel upon land not already containing the watercourse, subject to the landowner receiving compensation for the land occupied by the new channel and for any damages, as provided under the law of eminent domain.

---------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-206(1): (2) Subject to Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-206(2): If a drainage district is located in more than one county, a county legislative body may not appoint more than two members.


Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-207 Public highways, roads, or streets or railroad rights-of-way benefitted by district works.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
If a drainage district board of trustees determines that a public highway, road, street, or railroad right-of-way is or will be benefitted by district drainage canals or other works that have been or will be constructed:Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-207(1): the district shall assess benefits and taxes against the public highway, road, street, or railroad right-of-way in the same manner as if the highway, road, street, or railroad right-of-way were in private ownership;
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-207(2): the district may treat the highway, road, street, or railroad right-of-way the same as it would treat private land; and
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-207(3): the state or local entity having control of the public highway, road, or street or the owner of the railroad right-of-way shall pay the applicable taxes assessed against the land, whether or not it owns the fee simple title to the land covered by the highway, road, street, or railroad right-of-way.

Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-208(2)(b)(ii): at points that are indicated by a competent drainage engineer.

Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-211 Penalty for wrongfully damaging a district work.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-211(1): A person who wrongfully and purposely fills, cuts, injures, destroys, or impairs the usefulness of a drain, ditch, or other work of a drainage district is guilty of a class C misdemeanor.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-211(2): Each person who negligently, wrongfully, or purposely fills, cuts, injures, destroys, or impairs the usefulness of a drain, ditch, levee, or other work of a drainage district or obstructs or fills any natural stream or outlet used by a drainage district, whether inside or outside the district, shall be liable to the district for all resulting damages.

Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-504 Irrigation district board of trustees -- Bond for board of trustees members and district if the district is appointed as fiscal or other agent for the United States.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-504(1): 17B-2a-505
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-504(1)(a): 17B-2a-505 One board of trustees member shall be elected from each division established as provided in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-504(1)(b): Each landowner within an irrigation district may vote for one board of trustees member for the division in which the landowner's land is located.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-504(1)(c): Each landowner is entitled to cast one vote for each acre-foot or fraction of an acre-foot of water allotted to the land owned by the landowner.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-504(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-504(2)(a): If an irrigation district is appointed fiscal agent of the United States or is authorized by the United States to collect money on behalf of the United States with respect to a federal project:
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-504(2)(a)(i): each member of the district's board of trustees shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-504(2)(a)(i)(A): execute an official bond in the amount required by the Secretary of the Interior, conditioned upon the faithful discharge of the trustee's duties; and
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-504(2)(a)(i)(B): file the official bond in the office of the clerk of the county in which the district is located; and
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-504(2)(a)(ii): the irrigation district shall execute an additional bond for the district's faithful discharge of its duties as fiscal or other agent of the United States.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-504(2)(b): The United States or any person injured by the failure of a member of the board of trustees or of the district to perform fully, promptly, and completely a duty may sue upon the official bond.


Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-505 Divisions.
-------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-505(1): The board of trustees of each irrigation district shall divide the district into divisions, each as nearly equal in size to the others as practicable.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-505(2): The number of divisions shall be equal to the number of board of trustees members.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-505(3): Chapter 1, Part 4, Annexation; Chapter 1, Part 5, Withdrawal At least 30 days before an election of board of trustees members, the board shall redivide the district into divisions if, since the last time the board divided the district into divisions:
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-505(3)(a): Chapter 1, Part 4, Annexation the district has annexed land under
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-505(3)(b): Chapter 1, Part 5, Withdrawal land has been withdrawn from the district under
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-505(3)(c): the number of board of trustees members has been changed.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-507 Right-of-way over state land.
--------------------------------------------------------------
Each irrigation district has a right-of-way on land that is or becomes the property of the state to locate, construct, and maintain district works.

Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-508 Inclusion of state land in an irrigation district.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-508(1): State land that is not under a contract of sale may be included in an irrigation district upon petition by the state entity responsible for the administration of the land.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-508(2): State land included in an irrigation district may not be:
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-508(2)(a): assessed by the district; or
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-508(2)(b): the subject of use charges imposed by the district.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-508(3): The entity responsible for the administration of the state land to be included in an irrigation district and the state engineer shall make a thorough examination of the benefits to accrue to the land by its inclusion in the district and by the acquisition of water rights for the land.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-508(4): (3); (4)(a)
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-508(4)(a): (3) The entity responsible for the administration of the state land to be included in an irrigation district may enter into a contract with the district, specifying the land benefitted and the amount of benefit, as determined under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-508(4)(b): (4)(a) Each contract under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-508(4)(c): The entity responsible for the administration of state land included in an irrigation district may, at its option, pay the full amount of the contract at any time.


Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-509 State engineer not prohibited from increasing water allotment.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Nothing in this part may be construed to prohibit the state engineer, upon petition by an irrigation district board of trustees, from increasing the maximum allotment of water for one or more tracts of land within the district if the state engineer determines that the land cannot be beneficially irrigated with the currently allotted water.

Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-510 Rules for the distribution and use of water.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-510(1): Each irrigation district board of trustees shall establish equitable rules for the distribution and use of water among the owners of land in the district.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-510(2): (1) The board of trustees of an irrigation district that establishes rules under Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-511 Distribution of water under a contract with the United States.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
If an irrigation district acquires the right to use water under a contract with the United States, the district shall distribute and apportion water according to the contract and federal law, rules, and regulations.

Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-512 Removal of land from the assessor's roll.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-512(1): An irrigation district may direct a county treasurer to remove parcels of land from the district's billing if:
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-512(1)(a): the land is publicly dedicated to a street, highway, or road; or
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-512(1)(b): the use of the land has so permanently changed as to prevent the beneficial use of water on it.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-512(2): (1) Each county treasurer shall comply with the direction of an irrigation district under Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-513 Temporary application of water to land.
------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-513(1): Upon the written application of the owner of land that has no water allotment or an insufficient water allotment, an irrigation district board of trustees may temporarily permit water to be applied to the land and charge the owner for that water.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-513(2): (1) Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-514 Assignment of the right to water.
------------------------------------------------------------------
With the consent of the irrigation district board of trustees, a landowner in the district may assign the right to some or all of the water apportioned to the landowner's land for any one year to another bona fide landowner in the district for use in the district, if all charges for the water have been paid.

Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-515 Distribution of water when supply is inadequate.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------
If an irrigation district's water supply is not sufficient to supply all the needs within the district, the board of trustees may distribute water as the board considers best for all concerned, subject to distribution and apportionment requirements of a district contract with the United States and applicable federal law, rule, and regulation.

Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-516 Diversions of water subject to eminent domain law.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Nothing in this part may be construed to authorize any person to divert the water of a river, creek, stream, canal, or reservoir to the detriment of anyone having a prior right to the water, unless compensation is previously determined and paid according to the laws of eminent domain.

Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-705(5): The board of trustees shall canvass the votes cast at the election, and, if a majority of the votes cast are in favor of the imposition of the tax, the district is authorized to impose an additional levy to raise the additional amount of money required.


Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-706 Definitions -- Notice of intent to commence ultra-low volume treatment -- Exceptions.

Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-801 Title.
---------------------------------------
This part is known as the "Public Transit District Act."

Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-802 Definitions.
---------------------------------------------
As used in this part:Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-802(1): "Affordable housing" means housing occupied or reserved for occupancy by households that meet certain gross household income requirements based on the area median income for households of the same size.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-802(1)(a): "Affordable housing" may include housing occupied or reserved for occupancy by households that meet specific area median income targets or ranges of area median income targets.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-802(1)(b): "Affordable housing" does not include housing occupied or reserved for occupancy by households with gross household incomes that are more than 60% of the area median income for households of the same size.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-802(2): "Appointing entity" means the person, county, unincorporated area of a county, or municipality appointing a member to a public transit district board of trustees.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-802(3): 17B-2a-810; 17B-2a-811
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-802(3)(a): "Chief executive officer" means a person appointed by the board of trustees of a small public transit district to serve as chief executive officer.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-802(3)(b): 17B-2a-810; 17B-2a-811 "Chief executive officer" shall enjoy all the rights, duties, and responsibilities defined in Sections
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-802(4): "Confidential employee" means a person who, in the regular course of the person's duties:
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-802(4)(a): assists in and acts in a confidential capacity in relation to other persons who formulate, determine, and effectuate management policies regarding labor relations; or
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-802(4)(b): has authorized access to information relating to effectuating or reviewing the employer's collective bargaining policies.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-802(5): "Council of governments" means a decision-making body in each county composed of membership including the county governing body and the mayors of each municipality in the county.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-802(6): 72-1-201 "Department" means the Department of Transportation created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-802(7): "Executive director" means a person appointed by the board of trustees of a large public transit district to serve as executive director.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-802(8): 59-12-102 "Fixed guideway" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-802(9): 72-1-102 "Fixed guideway capital development" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-802(10): 17B-2a-810; 17B-2a-811
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-802(10)(a): "General manager" means a person appointed by the board of trustees of a small public transit district to serve as general manager.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-802(10)(b): 17B-2a-810; 17B-2a-811 "General manager" shall enjoy all the rights, duties, and responsibilities defined in Sections
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-802(11): "Large public transit district" means a public transit district that provides public transit to an area that includes:
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-802(11)(a): more than 65% of the population of the state based on the most recent official census or census estimate of the United States Census Bureau; and
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-802(11)(b): two or more counties.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-802(12): 
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-802(12)(a): "Locally elected public official" means a person who holds an elected position with a county or municipality.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-802(12)(b): "Locally elected public official" does not include a person who holds an elected position if the elected position is not with a county or municipality.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-802(13): "Managerial employee" means a person who is:
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-802(13)(a): engaged in executive and management functions; and
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-802(13)(b): charged with the responsibility of directing, overseeing, or implementing the effectuation of management policies and practices.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-802(14): 72-1-208.5 "Metropolitan planning organization" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-802(15): "Multicounty district" means a public transit district located in more than one county.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-802(16): "Operator" means a public entity or other person engaged in the transportation of passengers for hire.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-802(17): 
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-802(17)(a): "Public transit" means regular, continuing, shared-ride, surface transportation services that are open to the general public or open to a segment of the general public defined by age, disability, or low income.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-802(17)(b): "Public transit" does not include transportation services provided by:
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-802(17)(b)(i): chartered bus;
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-802(17)(b)(ii): sightseeing bus;
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-802(17)(b)(iii): taxi;
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-802(17)(b)(iv): school bus service;
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-802(17)(b)(v): courtesy shuttle service for patrons of one or more specific establishments; or
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-802(17)(b)(vi): intra-terminal or intra-facility shuttle services.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-802(18): "Public transit district" means a special district that provides public transit services.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-802(19): "Small public transit district" means any public transit district that is not a large public transit district.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-802(20): 10-9a-403.1 "Station area plan" means a plan developed and adopted by a municipality in accordance with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-802(21): (21)(a)
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-802(21)(a): "Supervisor" means a person who has authority, in the interest of the employer, to:
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-802(21)(a)(i): hire, transfer, suspend, lay off, recall, promote, discharge, assign, reward, or discipline other employees; or
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-802(21)(a)(ii): adjust another employee's grievance or recommend action to adjust another employee's grievance.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-802(21)(b): (21)(a) "Supervisor" does not include a person whose exercise of the authority described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-802(21)(b)(i): is of a merely routine or clerical nature; and
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-802(21)(b)(ii): does not require the person to use independent judgment.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-802(22): "Transit facility" means a transit vehicle, transit station, depot, passenger loading or unloading zone, parking lot, or other facility:
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-802(22)(a): leased by or operated by or on behalf of a public transit district; and
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-802(22)(b): related to the public transit services provided by the district, including:
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-802(22)(b)(i): railway or other right-of-way;
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-802(22)(b)(ii): railway line; and
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-802(22)(b)(iii): a reasonable area immediately adjacent to a designated stop on a route traveled by a transit vehicle.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-802(23): "Transit vehicle" means a passenger bus, coach, railcar, van, or other vehicle operated as public transportation by a public transit district.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-802(24): "Transit-oriented development" means a mixed use residential or commercial area that is designed to maximize access to public transit and includes the development of land owned by a large public transit district.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-802(25): "Transit-supportive development" means a mixed use residential or commercial area that is designed to maximize access to public transit and does not include the development of land owned by a large public transit district.

Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-805 Limitations on authority of a public transit district.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-805(1): A public transit district may not exercise control over a transit facility or public transit service or system owned or operated inside or outside the district by a governmental entity unless, upon mutually agreeable terms, the governmental entity consents.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-805(2): (2); (2); Title 72, Chapter 12, Travel Reduction Act
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-805(2)(a): A public transit district may not establish, directly or indirectly, a public transit service or system, or acquire a facility necessary or incidental to a public transit service or system, in a manner or form that diverts, lessens, or competes for the patronage or revenue of a preexisting system of a publicly or privately owned public carrier furnishing like service, unless the district obtains the consent of the publicly or privately owned carrier.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-805(2)(b): (2) A public transit district's maintenance and operation of an existing system that the district acquires from a publicly or privately owned public carrier may not be considered to be the establishment of a public transit service or system under this Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-805(2)(c): (2); Title 72, Chapter 12, Travel Reduction Act A public transit district's introduction, maintenance, or operation of a system may not be considered to be the establishment of a public transit service or system under this Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-805(2)(c)(i): as part of a program of projects approved by the Federal Transit Administration;
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-805(2)(c)(ii): in cooperation with the state or a political subdivision of the state, pursuant to an interlocal agreement; or
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-805(2)(c)(iii): Title 72, Chapter 12, Travel Reduction Act in accordance with

Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-811 General manager or chief executive officer of a small public transit district.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-811(1): (2); (3); (4)
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-811(1)(a): The board of trustees of a small public transit district shall appoint a person as a general manager.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-811(1)(b): The board of trustees of a small public transit district may, at its discretion, appoint a person as a chief executive officer.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-811(1)(c): (2) The board of trustees of a small public transit district shall allocate the responsibilities defined in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-811(1)(d): (3); (4) The chief executive officer shall have the same rights allocated to the general manager under Subsections
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-811(1)(e): The appointment of a general manager, chief executive officer, or both, shall be by the affirmative vote of a majority of all members of the board of trustees.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-811(1)(f): The board's appointment of a person as general manager, chief executive officer, or both, shall be based on the person's qualifications, with special reference to the person's actual experience in or knowledge of accepted practices with respect to the duties of the office.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-811(1)(g): A person appointed as general manager or chief executive officer of a small public transit district is not required to be a resident of the state at the time of appointment.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-811(2): A general manager or chief executive officer of a small public transit district shall have the following responsibilities as allocated by the board of trustees:
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-811(2)(a): be a full-time officer and devote full time to the district's business;
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-811(2)(b): ensure that all district ordinances are enforced;
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-811(2)(c): prepare and submit to the board of trustees, as soon as practical but not less than 45 days after the end of each fiscal year, a complete report on the district's finances and administrative activities for the preceding year;
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-811(2)(d): keep the board of trustees advised as to the district's needs;
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-811(2)(e): prepare or cause to be prepared all plans and specifications for the construction of district works;
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-811(2)(f): cause to be installed and maintained a system of auditing and accounting that completely shows the district's financial condition at all times; and
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-811(2)(g): attend meetings of the board of trustees.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-811(3): (5) A general manager of a small public transit district:
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-811(3)(a): serves at the pleasure of the board of trustees;
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-811(3)(b): holds office for an indefinite term;
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-811(3)(c): (5) may be removed by the board of trustees upon the adoption of a resolution by the affirmative vote of a majority of all members of the board, subject to Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-811(3)(d): has full charge of:
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-811(3)(d)(i): the acquisition, construction, maintenance, and operation of district facilities; and
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-811(3)(d)(ii): the administration of the district's business affairs;
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-811(3)(e): is entitled to participate in the deliberations of the board of trustees as to any matter before the board; and
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-811(3)(f): may not vote at a meeting of the board of trustees.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-811(4): The board of trustees may not reduce the general manager's salary below the amount fixed at the time of original appointment unless:
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-811(4)(a): the board adopts a resolution by a vote of a majority of all members; and
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-811(4)(b): if the general manager demands in writing, the board gives the general manager the opportunity to be publicly heard at a meeting of the board before the final vote on the resolution reducing the general manager's salary.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-811(5): (3)(c); (5)(a); (5)(a)(ii)

Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-811.1 Executive director of a large public transit district.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-811.1(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-811.1(1)(a): The board of trustees of a large public transit district shall appoint a person as an executive director.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-811.1(1)(b): The appointment of an executive director shall be by the affirmative vote of a majority of the board of trustees.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-811.1(1)(c): The board's appointment of a person as executive director shall be based on the person's qualifications, with special reference to the person's actual experience in or knowledge of accepted practices with respect to the duties of the office.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-811.1(1)(d): A person appointed as executive director of a large public transit district is not required to be a resident of the state at the time of appointment.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-811.1(2): An executive director of a large public transit district shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-811.1(2)(a): be a full-time officer and devote full time to the district's business;
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-811.1(2)(b): serve at the pleasure of the board of trustees;
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-811.1(2)(c): hold office for an indefinite term;
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-811.1(2)(d): ensure that all district ordinances are enforced;
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-811.1(2)(e): prepare and submit to the board of trustees, as soon as practical but not less than 45 days after the end of each fiscal year, a complete report on the district's finances and administrative activities for the preceding year;
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-811.1(2)(f): advise the board of trustees regarding the needs of the district;
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-811.1(2)(g): in consultation with the board of trustees, prepare or cause to be prepared all plans and specifications for the construction of district works;
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-811.1(2)(h): cause to be installed and maintained a system of auditing and accounting that completely shows the district's financial condition at all times;
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-811.1(2)(i): attend meetings of the board of trustees;
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-811.1(2)(j): in consultation with the board of trustees, have charge of:
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-811.1(2)(j)(i): the acquisition, construction, maintenance, and operation of district facilities; and
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-811.1(2)(j)(ii): the administration of the district's business affairs; and
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-811.1(2)(k): be entitled to participate in the deliberations of the board of trustees as to any matter before the board.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-811.1(3): The board of trustees may not remove the executive director or reduce the executive director's salary below the amount fixed at the time of original appointment unless:
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-811.1(3)(a): the board adopts a resolution by a vote of a majority of all members; and
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-811.1(3)(b): if the executive director demands in writing, the board gives the executive director the opportunity to be publicly heard at a meeting of the board before the final vote on the resolution removing the executive director or reducing the executive director's salary.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-811.1(4): (3); (4)(a); (4)(a)(ii)

Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-812 Comptroller required to provide statement of revenues and expenditures.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
The comptroller of each public transit district shall, as soon as possible after the close of each fiscal year:Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-812(1): prepare a statement of revenues and expenditures for the fiscal year just ended, in the detail that the board of trustees prescribes; and
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-812(2): transmit a copy of the statement to the chief executive officer of:
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-812(2)(a): each municipality within the district; and
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-812(2)(b): each county with unincorporated area within the district.


Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-813 Rights, benefits, and protective conditions for employees of a public transit district -- Strike prohibited -- Employees of an acquired transit system.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-813(1): As used in this section:
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-813(1)(a): 
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-813(1)(a)(i): "Employee" means an individual employed by an employer.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-813(1)(a)(ii): "Employee" does not include a person employed as a supervisor, managerial employee, or confidential employee.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-813(1)(b): "Employer" means a person that employs an employee.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-813(2): The rights, benefits, and other employee protective conditions and remedies of Section 13(c) of the Urban Mass Transportation Act of 1964, 49 U.S.C. Sec. 5333(b), as determined by the Secretary of Labor, apply to a public transit district's establishment and operation of a public transit service or system.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-813(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-813(3)(a): Employees of a public transit system established and operated by a public transit district have the right to:
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-813(3)(a)(i): self-organization;
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-813(3)(a)(ii): form, join, or assist labor organizations; and
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-813(3)(a)(iii): bargain collectively through representatives of their own choosing.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-813(3)(b): Employees of a public transit district and labor organizations may not join in a strike against the public transit system operated by the public transit district.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-813(3)(c): Each public transit district shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-813(3)(c)(i): recognize and bargain exclusively with any labor organization representing a majority of the district's employees in an appropriate unit with respect to wages, salaries, hours, working conditions, and welfare, pension, and retirement provisions; and
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-813(3)(c)(ii): upon reaching agreement with the labor organization, enter into and execute a written contract incorporating the agreement.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-813(4): If a public transit district acquires an existing public transit system:
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-813(4)(a): all employees of the acquired system who are necessary for the operation of the acquired system, except executive and administrative officers and employees, shall be:
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-813(4)(a)(i): transferred to and appointed employees of the acquiring public transit district; and
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-813(4)(a)(ii): given sick leave, seniority, vacation, and pension or retirement credits in accordance with the acquired system's records;
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-813(4)(b): members and beneficiaries of a pension or retirement plan or other program of benefits that the acquired system has established shall continue to have rights, privileges, benefits, obligations, and status with respect to that established plan or program; and
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-813(4)(c): the public transit district may establish, amend, or modify, by agreement with employees or their authorized representatives, the terms, conditions, and provisions of a pension or retirement plan or of an amendment or modification of a pension or retirement plan.

Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-815 Rates and charges for service -- Fare collection information private.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-815(1): The board of trustees of a public transit district shall fix rates and charges for service provided by the district by a two-thirds vote of all board members.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-815(2): Rates and charges shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-815(2)(a): be reasonable; and
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-815(2)(b): to the extent practicable:
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-815(2)(b)(i): result in enough revenue to make the public transit system self supporting; and
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-815(2)(b)(ii): be sufficient to:
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-815(2)(b)(ii)(A): pay for district operating expenses;
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-815(2)(b)(ii)(B): provide for repairs, maintenance, and depreciation of works and property that the district owns or operates;
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-815(2)(b)(ii)(C): provide for the purchase, lease, or acquisition of property and equipment;
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-815(2)(b)(ii)(D): pay the interest and principal of bonds that the district issues; and
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-815(2)(b)(ii)(E): pay for contracts, agreements, leases, and other legal liabilities that the district incurs.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-815(3): 63G-2-302; Title 63G, Chapter 2, Government Records Access and Management Act; (3); 63G-2-202
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-815(3)(a): 63G-2-302; Title 63G, Chapter 2, Government Records Access and Management Act In accordance with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-815(3)(a)(i): travel data, including:
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-815(3)(a)(i)(A): the identity of the purchasing individual or entity;
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-815(3)(a)(i)(B): travel dates, times, or frequency of use; and
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-815(3)(a)(i)(C): locations of use;
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-815(3)(a)(ii): service type or vehicle identification used by the customer;
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-815(3)(a)(iii): the unique transit pass identifier assigned to the customer; or
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-815(3)(a)(iv): customer account information, including the cardholder's name, the credit or debit card number, the card issuer identification, or any other related information.

Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-816(3)(b)(iv): rebut evidence introduced by others;

Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-816(3)(d): technical rules of evidence need not be followed, regardless of the existence of a common law or statutory rule that makes improper the admission of evidence over objection in a civil action;

Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-827 Integration of public transit services and facilities.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-827(1): If a public transit district provides public transit services in an area that is adjacent to or overlaps with an area in which public transit services are also provided by another public transit provider, including a public-private partnership entity, the public transit district and the public transit provider entity shall ensure that:
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-827(1)(a): any public transit facilities of one provider connect with the public transit facilities of the other provider;
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-827(1)(b): the schedules of all relevant public transit providers are coordinated as one public transit system; and
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-827(1)(c): 
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-827(1)(c)(i): if both public transit providers collect a fare directly from public transit passengers, an integrated and uniform fare system is implemented across the coordinated public transit system; and
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-827(1)(c)(ii): the revenue generated from the uniform fare system is equitably divided among the public transit providers according to service provided and mileage covered.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-827(2): A public transit district and a public transit provider, including a public-private partnership entity, may negotiate the ability of one public transit provider to operate on the transit facilities of the other public transit provider.
Utah Code Annotated § 17B-2a-827(3): (1); (3)(a)
